**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:

This separates policy actions from personal news, a crucial distinction for strategic response planning.

For instance, "President Trump's Lawsuits Against Media Outlets" became the more specific "President Trump's Libel Lawsuits," and "Legislative Activity & Voting Records" is now "Legislative Activity & Key Votes." 5.  **Enhanced Logical Flow:** The overall structure now flows from the dominant news cycle (Epstein), to the actions of the federal government (Executive, Foreign Policy, Congress), down to the state level, and finishes with the broader context of media and the President's personal profile. This hierarchical organization is more intuitive.

President Trump has launched a significant legal offensive against some of the country's most prominent news organizations. The lawsuits stem directly from a Wall Street Journal "expose" concerning an alleged birthday letter or card connected to Jeffrey Epstein [4]. **Area 1: The Epstein Scandal: Investigations and Political Fallout**

**Topic 1.1: President Trump Initiates Libel Lawsuits Against Major Media**
President Trump has launched a significant legal offensive against some of the country's most prominent news organizations. He has initiated libel lawsuits targeting Dow Jones, its parent company News Corp, executive chairman Rupert Murdoch, and specific reporters at the Wall Street Journal [1]. Court records confirm the legal action with a docket titled "Trump v. Murdoch" [2]. The lawsuits stem directly from a Wall Street Journal "expose" concerning an alleged birthday letter or card connected to Jeffrey Epstein [3]. This direct legal challenge represents a major escalation in the administration's contentious relationship with the press and an aggressive strategy to control the narrative surrounding the Epstein matter.

[1] Donald Trump sues Dow Jones, News Corp, Rupert Murdoch, WSJ reporters for libel, court records show, https://www.reuters.com/legal/government/donald-trump-sues-dow-jones-news-corp-rupert-murdoch-wsj-reporters-libel-court-2025-07-18/

**Topic 1.2: DOJ and FBI Actions on Case Files Intensify Scrutiny**

This briefing synthesizes critical developments over the past 24 hours. The nation is witnessing a significant expansion of executive power alongside escalating legal and political challenges centered on the administration. Key events include direct legal action by the President against major media outlets, Department of Justice moves to contain the fallout from the Epstein case, and a series of transformative domestic policy changes affecting civil rights, environmental regulation, and federal governance. These events demand immediate and coordinated attention.

**Area 1: The Epstein Scandal: Investigations and Political Fallout**

**Topic 1.1: President Trump Initiates Libel Lawsuits Against Major Media**
President Trump has launched a significant legal offensive against some of the country's most prominent news organizations. He has initiated libel lawsuits targeting Dow Jones, its parent company News Corp, executive chairman Rupert Murdoch, and specific reporters at the Wall Street Journal [1]. Court records confirm the legal action with a docket titled "Trump v. Murdoch" [2]. The lawsuits stem directly from a Wall Street Journal "expose" concerning an alleged birthday letter or card connected to Jeffrey Epstein [3]. This direct legal challenge represents a major escalation in the administration's contentious relationship with the press and an aggressive strategy to control the narrative surrounding the Epstein matter.

### 1.1. President Trump Initiates Libel Lawsuits Against Major Media

The lawsuits stem directly from a Wall Street Journal "expose" concerning an alleged birthday letter or card connected to Jeffrey Epstein [3]. This direct legal challenge represents a major escalation in the administration's contentious relationship with the press and an aggressive strategy to control the narrative surrounding the Epstein matter.

The public and political discourse surrounding the Epstein files has grown increasingly volatile and polarized. President Trump himself has publicly claimed the files are "faked," a statement that media outlets are contrasting with reports that many of the associated documents have been public for years [1]. Meanwhile, Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard, facing continued criticism over the matter, has deflected by alleging the existence of a "Russia ‘Conspiracy’" [2]. On the President’s behalf, Representative Marjorie Taylor Greene has mounted a vigorous defense of his past friendship with Epstein. She attacked what she called "fake outrage" from Democrats calling for the files' release, specifically targeting their support for LGBTQ+ people and "drag queen story time" [3].

## 2. Trump Administration: Domestic Policy & Executive Actions

### 2.1. Immigration Enforcement and Legal Challenges
The administration’s hardline immigration policies are triggering significant legal battles and public controversies. A new lawsuit has been filed on behalf of young immigrants who, after facing abuse and neglect, now claim the administration has exposed them to deportation [1]. At the same time, the Department of Homeland Security (DHS) has reportedly classified the act of filming ICE officers as a "violent tactic," a move that could have broad implications for press freedom and public oversight [2]. Adding to the controversy, Secretary of Homeland Security Kristi Noem allegedly "threaten[ed]" a reporter who asked about the potential for racial profiling by ICE agents [3]. In Congress, a State Department official testified about Stephen Miller's involvement in discussions regarding student visas and antisemitism [4]. The head of ICE has also confirmed that the agency uses Medicaid data for its operations, and an unnamed GOP Senator publicly advised U.S. citizens, "'Don't Hang Around Illegals' If You Don't Want to Be Detained" [5, 6].

### 2.2. Sweeping Changes to Social, Civil Rights, and Gun Policies
The administration is advancing a series of policies with profound impacts on social and civil rights issues, prompting the Urban League to declare a national "'State of Emergency' for Civil Rights" [1]. The Office of Personnel Management has set a deadline for a "government-wide purge of transgender and nonbinary inclusion," with one report labeling the OPM the new "enforcement arm of Trump’s anti-LGBTQ+ agenda" [2]. This follows the shutdown of the LGBTQ-specific option on the 988 crisis lifeline, a resource that gave queer youth "immediate access to trained counselors" [3]. Further actions include preparations to drop seven major housing discrimination cases and a plan to destroy nearly $10 million worth of contraceptives [4, 5]. Countering these moves, a federal judge has cited the President's "Gender Edicts" in a ruling to halt the deportation of a non-binary American [6]. Separately, the administration has proposed a "major change to gun laws," though the specific content of this proposal is not detailed in the headlines [7].

### 2.3. Economic, Environmental, and Energy Regulation
Significant regulatory shifts are underway across key sectors of the economy and environment. The Environmental Protection Agency (E.P.A.) has formally announced its intent to completely eliminate its scientific research arm, a foundational move that would fundamentally alter the agency's ability to conduct science-based policymaking [1]. In a landmark move for the financial technology sector, President Trump has signed the "GENIUS Act" into law, which is being hailed as the first major crypto bill [2]. In the automotive sector, administration regulators are moving to zero out all fuel economy fines retroactively to the 2022 model year, a significant boon for automakers [3]. In agriculture, the USDA has abruptly canceled a $30 million grant that was intended to bolster local food production in Hawaiʻi [4]. These individual actions are taking place against the backdrop of what one analysis calls a broader "war on climate-conscious investing" being waged from the right [5].

### 2.4. Federal Governance and Justice System Actions
President Trump has taken steps to reshape the federal government itself, issuing an executive order that "creates a new classification of federal employees" [1]. The specifics of this change are not yet public, but it could represent a historic alteration of the civil service. In the justice system, the administration is reportedly advocating for a minimal one-day sentence for the police officer convicted in the 2020 killing of Breonna Taylor [2]. On the political-legal front, Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard made a public call for the prosecution of former President Barack Obama, basing her demand on unspecified claims related to the 2016 election [3]. In a separate judicial matter, a court has dismissed a lawsuit the President filed against author Bob Woodward over an audiobook [4].

## 3. Foreign Policy & National Security

### 3.1. Diplomatic Relations and International Agreements
The administration executed a "major prisoner swap" involving Venezuela and El Salvador [1]. As a result of the deal, an unspecified number of Americans held in Venezuela have been freed. In a highly unusual exchange, El Salvador released hundreds of U.S. deportees from one of its "notorious prison[s]" as its part of the agreement [2]. This event showcases a transactional and unconventional diplomatic approach. In a potentially significant shift in official U.S. foreign policy posture, the administration has also issued a directive instructing American embassies worldwide to "rein in criticism of foreign elections," a move that could fundamentally alter America's role in global democracy promotion [3].

### 3.2. U.S. Alliances, Foreign Aid, and Political Developments
A weapons deal for Ukraine, advanced by the Trump administration through NATO, is generating a sharp political backlash from the President's own supporters [1]. Reports indicate "MAGA anger" over the deal, with proponents of the America First doctrine expressing sentiments such as "'Not our war.'" This highlights a significant ideological rift within the President's base on foreign intervention and aid. Meanwhile, regarding escalating tensions in the Middle East, Democratic Senator Chris Coons of Delaware has offered a notable perspective. He commented that recent U.S. strikes against Iran "could ultimately be a positive step," suggesting potential for some bipartisan support for a muscular posture, though the specifics of the strikes remain unclear from reports [2].

## 4. Media Landscape & Public Discourse

### 4.1. Media Industry Shifts and Freedom of Speech Concerns
The abrupt cancellation of the television program "The Late Show with Stephen Colbert" is being widely interpreted as a significant moment for the American media landscape. One analysis frames the event as a direct consequence of political speech, stating: "Mock a Trump bribe on Monday, get canceled by Thursday," and concludes that this incident "reveals how billionaires and presidents are reshaping American media" [1]. A more cautious take from another outlet questions whether "money or politics" was the definitive cause, but ultimately concedes that the general "economics are tough for TV" across the board [2]. The incident has brought concerns about corporate influence and freedom of speech in media to the forefront of public debate.

## 5. Congressional & Partisan Politics

### 5.1. Legislative Activity and Bipartisan Votes
Despite heightened partisan tensions, the House of Representatives demonstrated overwhelming bipartisanship on a key national security issue. A measure introduced by Representative Marjorie Taylor Greene seeking to cut U.S. missile defense aid for Israel was decisively rejected by a vote of 422-6 [1]. In other legislative activity, members of the House are moving to codify recent executive actions into federal law. Two bills have been introduced for this purpose: H.R. 4534 aims to enact Executive Order 14191, which is described as "expanding educational freedom and opportunity for families" [2]. A second bill, H.R. 4533, seeks to codify Executive Order 14172, though the headlines do not provide details on the substance of this order [3].

Public opinion polling reveals a complex and shifting political landscape. Surveys indicate a broad public appetite for a third political party, although there is no consensus on its leadership, with Elon Musk's potential involvement being unpopular [1]. Within the Democratic coalition, a new poll suggests that voters who sat out the 2024 election now express a desire for candidates positioned "further to the left," citing figures like Representative Alexandria Ocasio-Cortez and Senator Bernie Sanders as examples [2]. On a key administration policy, public opinion has reportedly "turned on Trump’s immigration strategy — mostly," suggesting his approach may be losing support [3]. In a sign of internal Democratic maneuvering, House Minority Leader Hakeem Jeffries met with progressive New York politician Zohran Mamdani but has thus far withheld his endorsement [4].

## 6. State & Local Governance

### 6.1. State-Level Policy and Budgetary Actions
States are pursuing sharply divergent policy Agendas. In a major effort to address household economic burdens, two states have taken significant action to relieve medical debt: Michigan's Governor Whitmer has erased $144 million in debt for over 210,000 residents, and Arizona has bought back an even larger sum of $429 million for its citizens [1, 2]. Conversely, Puerto Rico has enacted a restrictive new law that criminalizes the provision of hormone therapy and gender-affirming surgery for any transgender individuals under the age of 21 [3]. In Florida, Governor DeSantis is facing scrutiny for fiscal management; he is publicly defending the use of Everglades restoration money for an immigrant detention center, while a separate report indicates that taxpayer funds intended for hurricane response and disaster preparedness were used to finance a project dubbed "'Alligator Alcatraz'" [4, 5].

### 6.2. Partisan Conflicts Over Redistricting
The high-stakes battle over political representation through redistricting is intensifying at the state level, with moves that will shape congressional maps for years to come. In a major victory for Republicans in a key battleground state, Florida's state justices have officially upheld a controversial redistricting map that was signed into law by Governor DeSantis. Opponents and one media outlet had decried the map as a "racist gerrymander" [1]. In a direct strategic response from the Democratic side, California Governor Gavin Newsom has announced that he wants his state to actively "counter Texas on redistricting," signaling a more aggressive, nationalized approach to the partisan gerrymandering wars [2].

## 7. President Trump: Personal Affairs

### 7.1. Scrutiny of President's Health and Past Statements
The White House has made a formal disclosure regarding President Trump's personal health, announcing that he has been diagnosed with a condition known as Chronic Venous Insufficiency. The announcement headline did not provide further details on the severity of the condition or its potential impact on his duties [1]. Separately, the President's past statements are facing renewed media scrutiny. His recent assertion that he has “never wrote a picture in my life” is being directly contradicted by outlets pointing to multiple instances of his sketches being sold at auction [2]. In another retrospective look, fact-checkers are investigating a February 2006 clip from 'The Howard Stern Show' in which Trump appeared to laughingly agree with being called a "'sexual predator'" during an episode reportedly "filled with jokes and laughter" [3].
